<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17385045417271020066">Years ago, Nora Bridge walked out on her marriage, leaving her daughters behind. Now she is a celebrity talk-show host. Her daughter Ruby is a struggling comedienne. The two haven’t spoken in more than a decade. Then a scandal from Nora’s past is exposed, and Ruby is offered a fortune to write a tell-all about her mother. Reluctantly she returns to the family house on Summ</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17385045417271020066">Years ago, Nora Bridge walked out on her marriage, leaving her daughters behind. Now she is a celebrity talk-show host. Her daughter Ruby is a struggling comedienne. The two haven’t spoken in more than a decade. Then a scandal from Nora’s past is exposed, and Ruby is offered a fortune to write a tell-all about her mother. Reluctantly she returns to the family house on Summer Island, a home filled with frayed memories of joy and heartache. Confronting a past that includes a never-forgotten love, a sick best friend, and a mother who has harbored terrible family secrets, Ruby finally begins to understand the complex ties that bind a mother and daughter—and the healing that comes with forgiveness.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/29992287?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 26, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1410084-mandy-sue" class="user" title="Mandy Sue">Mandy Sue</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/297135.Summer_Island" title="Paperback 9780345483447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1410084-mandy-sue?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1410084-mandy-sue?shelf=read-2009" class="actionLinkLite">read-2009</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer29992287">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12345393818668246827">Summer Island is a very touching story about the power of love through healing and forgiveness. It reminds us that each story has three sides and how sometimes we need to look past our own hurt and anger to renew an old relationship.<br /><br />Summer's Island is sold on it being a book about Mother/Daughter relationships but it is so much more. It is truths hidden behind masks; love lost yet still yearned for. It is pain from being apart from family; and resentment for losing so much time.<br /><br />Kristen Hannah on</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12345393818668246827">Summer Island is a very touching story about the power of love through healing and forgiveness. It reminds us that each story has three sides and how sometimes we need to look past our own hurt and anger to renew an old relationship.<br /><br />Summer's Island is sold on it being a book about Mother/Daughter relationships but it is so much more. It is truths hidden behind masks; love lost yet still yearned for. It is pain from being apart from family; and resentment for losing so much time.<br /><br />Kristen Hannah once again delivers a powerful story that anyone can relate too. Summer's Island is both sad and uplifting having you laugh and cry throughout the whole story and reaching for the phone to call someone you lost contact with when it is over.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_353703375">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353703375" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4525337-cathleen" class="left imgcol" title="Cathleen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439748657p2/4525337.jpg" alt="Cathleen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/353703375?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 31, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4525337-cathleen" class="user" title="Cathleen">Cathleen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/297135.Summer_Island" title="Paperback 9780345483447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4525337-cathleen?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer353703375">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer868723856417345836">I didn't have this book on my TBR list. I picked this up last weekend along with another book from this author. I started reading this Wednesday night. Massachusetts is having a heat wave and I do not have air conditioning. I thought this would be a good book to read during the hot, sticky and sleepless nights.<br /><br />I finished reading this story at 4:45 AM this morning. Some books should come with warning labels so you will know the story between the covers may cause you to feel a variety of emotions.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText868723856417345836">I didn't have this book on my TBR list. I picked this up last weekend along with another book from this author. I started reading this Wednesday night. Massachusetts is having a heat wave and I do not have air conditioning. I thought this would be a good book to read during the hot, sticky and sleepless nights.<br /><br />I finished reading this story at 4:45 AM this morning. Some books should come with warning labels so you will know the story between the covers may cause you to feel a variety of emotions. There were times I found my laughter or smile quickly changing to tears. <br /><br />This story is about a woman who walked away from her marriage and her 2 daughters. She becomes a radio celebrity with her own show. She gives advice to callers on a variety of issues. Then something from her past is made public and she becomes undesirable. She gets suspended from her talk show and her fans quickly turn their backs on her. She becomes the latest "news". <br /><br />She finds herself in the house she lived in with her husband and children. Her youngest daughter, who she had no contact with for many years, is staying with her. From that point on unfolds a story of a mother and a daughter trying to find a way to come to terms with each other and a past that caused so much pain. <br /><br />This is a remarkable story in so many ways. A family coming to terms with a painful past, secrets, forgiveness, rebuilding of relationship between a mother and her daughters, loss of a close family friend and the renewal of a childhood romance.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who enjoys this genre.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="868723856417345836">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_127784520">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127784520" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4459105-jessica-sinn-chick-lit-cafe" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica  Sinn (Chick Lit Cafe)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1364786417p2/4459105.jpg" alt="Jessica  Sinn (Chick Lit Cafe)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/127784520?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 24, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4459105-jessica-sinn-chick-lit-cafe" class="user" title="Jessica  Sinn (Chick Lit Cafe)">Jessica  Sinn (Chick Lit Cafe)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/297135.Summer_Island" title="Paperback 9780345483447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer127784520">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17846537818128190361">Nora Bridge had what appeared to be the American dream – a devoted husband, two loving daughters, and a quaint beachhouse on Summer Island. Yet one day she turned her back on them all and vanished into thin air.<br /><br /> A decade later her youngest daughter Ruby finds herself grappling with the heartbreaking legacy of her mother’s selfishness. Stuck in the spin cycle of financial and emotional debt, Ruby is listless, angry and desperate to make a buck. After Nora, ironically a nationally beloved radio ad</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17846537818128190361">Nora Bridge had what appeared to be the American dream – a devoted husband, two loving daughters, and a quaint beachhouse on Summer Island. Yet one day she turned her back on them all and vanished into thin air.<br /><br /> A decade later her youngest daughter Ruby finds herself grappling with the heartbreaking legacy of her mother’s selfishness. Stuck in the spin cycle of financial and emotional debt, Ruby is listless, angry and desperate to make a buck. After Nora, ironically a nationally beloved radio advice show host of “Family First,” becomes the center of a scandal, Ruby decides to make a quick buck by writing a tell-all roast about her absentee mother for a sleazy tabloid. <br /><br />Just when life couldn’t get worse for poor Nora, she wreaks her car in an alcohol-induced haze, rendering herself incapacitated in a wheelchair. Alone and helpless, she’s left to rely on the one person who despises her the most: Ruby.<br /><br />Guilted into taking care of her down-trodden mother at her childhood home in Summer Island, Ruby decides to maximize her quality time with mother dearest by writing her tell-all. But when her anger ebbs and forviness fights its way to the surface, she sruggles with the moral dilemma of cashing in on her mother’s scandal or killing the story and letting her mother back in her heart.<br /><br /> Lessons of redemption and second chances are also infused in the two subplots: one a romance between Ruby and Dean, an old boyfriend who she ditched after her mother left, and another involving Dean’s dying brother with only days left to make peace with his broken family. Conveniently they’re all summering on the island and rebuilding their relationships. <br /><br />Brimming with sentiments of forgiveness and unconditional love, the book reads like a lengthy episode of a Lifetime movie under the influence of “Delilah after Dark.” Get out those boxes of Kleenex ladies, this one is a surefired tearjerker.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17846537818128190361">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer129922468">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3774151630414502878">This is the first novel I have read by this author and I have to say I LOVED THIS BOOK - THANKS DONNA for the recommendation! What a wonderful story!!<br /><br />Nora Bridge is a radio talk show host that espouses the morals of a nation. People trust and love her. When pornographic pictures of her are released to the press, her carefully constructed world comes tumbling down around her and she is faced with the skeletons in her closet that have left her estranged from the two daughters she has loved from a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3774151630414502878">This is the first novel I have read by this author and I have to say I LOVED THIS BOOK - THANKS DONNA for the recommendation! What a wonderful story!!<br /><br />Nora Bridge is a radio talk show host that espouses the morals of a nation. People trust and love her. When pornographic pictures of her are released to the press, her carefully constructed world comes tumbling down around her and she is faced with the skeletons in her closet that have left her estranged from the two daughters she has loved from a distance for the past 11 years.<br /><br />The Journey back is a tumultuous one when Nora finds herself injured in a car accident and her daughter Ruby, who has nurtured her hatred since the day her mother left them, comes to care for her at the family home on Summer Island. The memories flood back and secrets are revealed that paint an entirely different picture of a time that Ruby was so sure of. Suffice it to say, things are not what she expected. <br /><br />This was a very good book with much more to the story than I have let on here. It is a tear-jerker and I spent the last few chapters with a box of tissues, so readers beware. I couldn't put this book down and I gave it 5 stars!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/357201400?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 28, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6032585-amanda-kimball" class="user" title="Amanda Kimball">Amanda Kimball</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/297135.Summer_Island" title="Paperback 9780345483447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer357201400">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer961573119489429734">I didn't have very high expectations for this book. I picked it up in a whim for $2, and it sat on my shelf for a good 4 months. What a wasted time! This book was wonderful. Complex and intellectually stimulating. I felt for Nora and was drawn to her despite her flaws. Ruby and Caro were definitely on opposite ends of the spectrum, but it worked so well. As a daughter and a sister, I could easily relate to pieces of them. You look at their family, their story, and see the good and the bad of you</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText961573119489429734">I didn't have very high expectations for this book. I picked it up in a whim for $2, and it sat on my shelf for a good 4 months. What a wasted time! This book was wonderful. Complex and intellectually stimulating. I felt for Nora and was drawn to her despite her flaws. Ruby and Caro were definitely on opposite ends of the spectrum, but it worked so well. As a daughter and a sister, I could easily relate to pieces of them. You look at their family, their story, and see the good and the bad of your own. You remember, if only for the moments you are reading, how precious family is and how quickly time passes, and you drift apart. It doesn't matter the intentions or the reasons, this book makes you want to call your loved ones just to take advantage of the moments you do have. Family is about fighting, forgiving, accepting, and loving; not only one another but yourself. I loved that Nora, despite her flaws, could see through the bad and help those in the wrong direction. I didn't feel she was a hypocrite, just lost on her journey to find herself, and make peace with her past.<br /><br />My favorite character was Eric. I loved his honesty and outlook on life. His character was deeply developed even though we didnt/couldn't interact with him the way we could the other characters. I wept for him. It's no surprise, we prepare for it all along, but you never think you will be so enveloped in a character until the final moments hit you. I hated his parents and their selfishness, but realize the gift that his suffering gave to Nora and Ruby. <br /><br />I would 100% recommend this novel to friends. This is definitely a keeper! I look forward to reading more by the author, and can't believe it's taken me so long to discover her.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="961573119489429734">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/2918559-renee" class="left imgcol" title="Renee"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1312337865p2/2918559.jpg" alt="Renee" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/159494363?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2918559-renee" class="user" title="Renee">Renee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/297135.Summer_Island" title="Paperback 9780345483447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer159494363">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer257482274760788452">Okay, I am at work, so I'll have to make this review short and to the point.<br /><br />This is the third Kristin Hannah book I have read, and while the first one was very touching ( <a title="True Colors by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975186.True_Colors">True Colors</a> ), the last two including this one, have been so-so.<br /><br />I begin to think these books are like Lifetime movies. I don't know why I would watch, they aren't particularly any good... and yet, it is easy to let a wasted few hours go by while a movie (book) full of cliches and emotional manipulation bumbles along. Sometimes</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText257482274760788452">Okay, I am at work, so I'll have to make this review short and to the point.<br /><br />This is the third Kristin Hannah book I have read, and while the first one was very touching ( <a title="True Colors by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3975186.True_Colors">True Colors</a> ), the last two including this one, have been so-so.<br /><br />I begin to think these books are like Lifetime movies. I don't know why I would watch, they aren't particularly any good... and yet, it is easy to let a wasted few hours go by while a movie (book) full of cliches and emotional manipulation bumbles along. Sometimes they can be touching, and other times I can literally feel braincells slowing down and dying off.<br /><br />This book was no different. The main character Ruby was so predictable as to be nearly one-dimensional. Of course she can't accept love. Of course she hates her mother. Of course she dyes her hair black and wears lots of eyeliner. Of course she feels betrayed by her mother, and therefore, she will betray her back. I was so worn sick and tired of Ruby that I could not even feel bad for her. And, as one would expect, she miraculously makes up with her mother and falls in love with a rich, successful man that sees through all her many (I do mean many!) emotional flaws and worships her anyway.<br /><br />Ugh. Like bad perfume - it was too cloying for me. Tried a tad too much. And, Hannah's attempt at adding humor fell short, very short. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="257482274760788452">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8043969861396336322">I waver between 4 and 5 stars on this one, but ultimately choose 5 because the story was wonderful, the character development was splendid and the story is one that is bound to stick with me for a long time. (6 months later I returned to this review and had actually entirely forgotten the story, so i reduced the rating to a 4)<br /><br />I read a version of this book which was released through epub, and thus there were some formatting and grammatical errors which were somewhat distracting, but the story sti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8043969861396336322">I waver between 4 and 5 stars on this one, but ultimately choose 5 because the story was wonderful, the character development was splendid and the story is one that is bound to stick with me for a long time. (6 months later I returned to this review and had actually entirely forgotten the story, so i reduced the rating to a 4)<br /><br />I read a version of this book which was released through epub, and thus there were some formatting and grammatical errors which were somewhat distracting, but the story still sucked me in. i found myself quickly unable to put this book down. so it was good that this was a quick read, taking less than 24 hours to finish.<br /><br />the story is reminiscent of a lifetime drama: a woman walks out of her marriage and is demonized by her two children. years later, her successful career veers off course and she finds herself recouping from a dui accident. her estranged youngest daughter returns under the guise of caring for her mother, but secretly plans to write a tell-all article about her. instead, the daughter learns to love and live again.<br /><br />while the dialogue does feel a little forced at times, and while the transition from hatred to love does seem to happen on a short time-line, this book teaches us the lesson that if we assume we have all the answers, we never really do.<br /><br />kudos to Kristin Hannah for such wonderful character development, and the reminder that sometimes fancy facades are placed over cracking foundations.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3853170795353605258">My 3 star rating is being generous on my part.<br /><br />This book was very predictable and cheesy beyond imagination.<br /><br />The character Ruby totally unbelievable. She goes from one personality to a completely different personality within a few weeks?<br /><br />The anger and family time lost could have most likely been eliminated if the mother would have written a letter to her daughters and explained in total honesty what happened to both her and her ex. What a self-centered woman!<br /><br />This book got the rating it did because when I got done reading it, I was so frustrated that I took my valuable time to read this predictable story with unlikeable characters.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText8186079677304410338">Feelings: pain, sadness, joyfulness <br /><br />I was hooked after the first 50 pages, even the night couldn't stop me. The story made me cry, I gasped for breath as I read some sentences, they touched my heart so deeply. Love and pain. Being loved and missing love. The non-expressed words are so painful, they torn apart and make devastation in hearts. I think my heart has not opened yet entirely, thus I was shocked as I was reading about Bridge family, their story, their feelings, their life were very heart-breaking to me, I couldn't escape from them, I had to read them in order to help to heal mine.<br /><br />In my family also there is a "scandalous" secret, some parts of it have already been unfolded, but painful emotions are still deeply buried inside our heart. Why? Because we are afraid of telling our feelings, our sorry-s, our I-love-you-s to each other, those moments makes us so vulnerable, and if the heart is not enough strong inside, the silence seems easier, but we should pay its price alter.<br /><br />This story still haunts me, and I want to reread some lines to understand my story better. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_152845950">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/152845950" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2690015-brenda" class="left imgcol" title="Brenda"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1251857476p2/2690015.jpg" alt="Brenda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/152845950?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 07, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2690015-brenda" class="user" title="Brenda">Brenda</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/297135.Summer_Island" title="Paperback 9780345483447" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer152845950">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2924513305269461281">It's rare that I find a fiction author whose books I sit down and devour for no other reason then they are a pure joy to read and whose characters I feel such a connection to. I loved her other books (Firefly Lane and True Colors) and this latest one I picked up from the library on a whim. It did not disappoint. The author is a Pacific NW native so many of the settings in her book are familiar places (in this case, the San Juan Islands). I typically end up crying at some point because the story</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2924513305269461281">It's rare that I find a fiction author whose books I sit down and devour for no other reason then they are a pure joy to read and whose characters I feel such a connection to. I loved her other books (Firefly Lane and True Colors) and this latest one I picked up from the library on a whim. It did not disappoint. The author is a Pacific NW native so many of the settings in her book are familiar places (in this case, the San Juan Islands). I typically end up crying at some point because the story has a tear jerker somewhere, but when I want an escape from reality, she is my go-to fiction author. This one was a quick 2-day read and I have 2 more of hers waiting in the wings when I need some "me time" to purely relax. Many fiction authors who release books on a frequent basis tend to have the same themes running throughout every book so you feel like no matter what you're reading, that you've already read it before. I don't find this with Kristin Hannah! I'm going to attend a book signing she's having locally later this month can't wait to meet her in person. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2924513305269461281">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/273429113?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2392166-megan-palasik" class="user" title="Megan Palasik">Megan Palasik</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8550472-summer-island" title="Audio CD 9781441840455" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2392166-megan-palasik?shelf=audio-book" class="actionLinkLite">audio-book</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer273429113">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8529996951207921178">I listened to this book as an audio book so my experience may be different than other readers'.<br /><br />The first book I ever read by Hannah was Night Road and I absolutely loved it! There was love, there was suspense, and I remember finishing it thinking, "Yes, here is a writer I can enjoy with Jodi Picoult (whom I love!)". <br /><br />So when I saw Summer Island at the library, I didn't hesitate to pick it up. I didn't even read the synopsis. Then I listened to the book.<br /><br />Firstly, the woman who read the book was won</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8529996951207921178">I listened to this book as an audio book so my experience may be different than other readers'.<br /><br />The first book I ever read by Hannah was Night Road and I absolutely loved it! There was love, there was suspense, and I remember finishing it thinking, "Yes, here is a writer I can enjoy with Jodi Picoult (whom I love!)". <br /><br />So when I saw Summer Island at the library, I didn't hesitate to pick it up. I didn't even read the synopsis. Then I listened to the book.<br /><br />Firstly, the woman who read the book was wonderful. She did the different voices well, (there were probably 10+ voices) and there were voice effects for when someone was on the phone and some others. I found those to be great effects and the reading was great. 5 stars for her.<br /><br />However, I wasn't particularly impressed with the story. I'm not one to predict or look ahead (mentally or physically with a book) in a story, but this one had me predicting the end from the very beginning. Instead of thinking, "Oh no, what will happen next?!?" I was thinking, "Ho hum, will she or won't she, what's their *secret* past, how much longer is on this disk?" <br /><br />If I hadn't known better, I would have thought this book was one of Hannah's earlier novels...when she was still getting her writing rhythm.<br /><br />It just became predictable in the end. Also, I thought the character of Caroline was underplayed and we never heard about what happened with her in the end. I almost found her character to be equally or more interesting than Ruby's.<br /><br />Overall I just wasn't impressed. It was a quick and easy read. Hannah does a great job describing scenes and fleshing out some characters, but the plot was predictable for me and I didn't feel connected enough to the characters in the end. No tears.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8529996951207921178">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4361930434577235868">After reading <a title="Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah">Kristin Hannah</a>'s books, she is definitely going to be my favourite author. Yes, after 6 books that I read from her.<br /><br />I would say, that I would give 3.5 stars to this one. At par with <a title="Night Road by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8949352.Night_Road">Night Road</a>, but not as emotional as <a title="Angel Falls by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/276342.Angel_Falls">Angel Falls</a> or <a title="Winter Garden by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6668467.Winter_Garden">Winter Garden</a>, which I consider is the best book to date by the author.<br /><br />Anyway, I have this kind of love-hate relationship with my mother. Maybe because my mom still treats me as a child, but at the same time, I know that she still loves me.<br /><br />It is kind of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4361930434577235868">After reading <a title="Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah">Kristin Hannah</a>'s books, she is definitely going to be my favourite author. Yes, after 6 books that I read from her.<br /><br />I would say, that I would give 3.5 stars to this one. At par with <a title="Night Road by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8949352.Night_Road">Night Road</a>, but not as emotional as <a title="Angel Falls by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/276342.Angel_Falls">Angel Falls</a> or <a title="Winter Garden by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6668467.Winter_Garden">Winter Garden</a>, which I consider is the best book to date by the author.<br /><br />Anyway, I have this kind of love-hate relationship with my mother. Maybe because my mom still treats me as a child, but at the same time, I know that she still loves me.<br /><br />It is kind of hard reading this book, I guess. Because the element of the mother and daughter is so strong that it affected me as a whole.<br /><br />Nora has not been in touch with her second daughter, Ruby for years. And her first daughter, Caro, their relationship is as threadbare as it can be. Because Nora decides to leave her family when both her daughters are teenagers.<br /><br />Thus start the heart wrenching emotional story. The impact of the relationship. How do you start to build back your daughter's trust? How would you mend pieces of your daughter's broken heart? And how would you tell your child never to end up like you? Alone even though you have lots of fame.<br /><br />Ruby thought she would revenge her mother when a scandal breaks out that tarnish her mother's reputation. They go back to Summer Island, where Ruby grows, because her mom is involved in an accident.<br /><br />There, she learns who Nora Bridge is, why she leaves her family. And it seems that not everything is black and white as what she first thinks, but grey seems the perfect colour to describe the blurry line of Ruby's perception and her mother's story.<br /><br />Ruby learns to love her mother again.<br /><br />Toward the end of the book, I become more emotional, with Eric's death and Ruby's finding herself. But most of all, the relationship between Nora, Ruby and Caro has finally mends - even though slowly, at first.<br /><br />"I love my mother," Ruby writes in her tell all confession.<br /><br />Yes, I love my mother.</span>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/772014-jenni?shelf=nook-books" class="actionLinkLite">nook-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer141506438">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16187691493422910366">This is the 10th Kristin Hannah I have read this year. I think I have mentioned a few times before that she and Jodi Picoult are probably my two favorite authors. They both have a style of writing that I am drawn to, and I have never been disappointed in any of their books.<br /><br />"Summer Island" was certainly no different. <br /><br /><a title="Summer Island by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/297135.Summer_Island">Summer Island</a> is about advice expert Nora Bridges, the two daughters she abandoned years ago (Ruby &amp; Caroline), and some other wonderful characters (Eric the homesexual cancer pa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16187691493422910366">This is the 10th Kristin Hannah I have read this year. I think I have mentioned a few times before that she and Jodi Picoult are probably my two favorite authors. They both have a style of writing that I am drawn to, and I have never been disappointed in any of their books.<br /><br />"Summer Island" was certainly no different. <br /><br /><a title="Summer Island by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/297135.Summer_Island">Summer Island</a> is about advice expert Nora Bridges, the two daughters she abandoned years ago (Ruby &amp; Caroline), and some other wonderful characters (Eric the homesexual cancer patient and his brother, Dean).<br /><br />I was completely sucked in from Page 1. The author has a way of making my feel very strongly about each of the characters. Nora becomes involved in a tabloid scandal, and she winds up being injured in a car accident -- her fault, because she was so depressed she drove in a drunk stupor right into a tree. When the tabloid scandal gets seriously revved up, Nora decides to hide away for a while at her old lake house. Her estranged daughter Ruby gets talked into caring for her injured mother for a week. <br /><br />I was surprised that this book make me so emotional, as I shed a lot of tears while reading -- especially in the last half. <br /><br />Obviously not wanting to reveal any spoilers, it was a book full of family, love, romance and sadness-- I loved it and can't wait to get started on my next Kristin Hannah book, <br /><a title="Distant Shores by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/836984.Distant_Shores">Distant Shores</a>.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1312090237">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3944781322045804886">I don't know. Maybe I just needed a good cry and didn't realize it.<br />I went into Summer Island, thinking along the lines of a good beach read story. Advise: Do NOT try reading this in public, unless you don't mind sharing tears while on display.<br />This one got to me.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText3944781322045804886">I don't know. Maybe I just needed a good cry and didn't realize it.<br />I went into Summer Island, thinking along the lines of a good beach read story. Advise: Do NOT try reading this in public, unless you don't mind sharing tears while on display.<br />This one got to me. It's the story of a mother and her two daughters and the ties that bind them...and the barriers that keep them apart.<br />Love, pain, disillusionment, relationships, pride, estrangement, marriage challenges, oh my... Ms Hannah includes everything and does it well. <br />Favorite quote (paraphrased): "I can't fully express how I feel about my mother. She is the keeper of my past. She knows the secret moments that have formed me. She is the one who held me,one last time as an unmarried young woman and whispered, 'I love you'. Will anyone else ever love me so unconditionally?"<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3944781322045804886">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer683985710">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17198056126693322800">All I can say about this book is WOW. I bought it purely to release as part of a BookCrossing Challenge, but couldn't let it out of my hands before I'd read it. I'm so glad I did.<br /><br />This is the story of Nora, a celebrity who preaches the sanctity of the family to millions of Americans via the radio and through magazines. But Nora walked out on her husband and her children, and now the press has proof she had an affair. Her career in ruins, she finds that she has no-one to turn too. <br /><br />Then there is Ru</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17198056126693322800">All I can say about this book is WOW. I bought it purely to release as part of a BookCrossing Challenge, but couldn't let it out of my hands before I'd read it. I'm so glad I did.<br /><br />This is the story of Nora, a celebrity who preaches the sanctity of the family to millions of Americans via the radio and through magazines. But Nora walked out on her husband and her children, and now the press has proof she had an affair. Her career in ruins, she finds that she has no-one to turn too. <br /><br />Then there is Ruby, her daughter. A struggling comic who uses her hatred of her Mum as the basis of her routine. She blames Nora for eveything and when she is offered a lot of money to write an expose, she jumps at the chance to hurt her mother back.<br /><br />They wind up back on Summer Island, the site of the family home, where Ruby learns that not everything was as rosy as she remembered it and her Mum is as human as anyone. Together, they also have to deal with the dying of an old friend and the return of the one man Ruby really ever loved.<br /><br />This is such a well-written, heart rendering story, and you can't help thinking about your own relationship with your Mother as you read. The big secrets aren't the only thing that keep you reading, as I was rooting for them both to reconcile at every turn of the page. I always think that a sign of a good book is when you're left crying at the end, and I was blubbing as well as the next person.<br /><br />I know that you're going to enjoy is.</span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer111567134">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14061894952572575529">For my book club this month. Nora is a discredited advice columnist (think Dr. Laura with a newspaper column and a radio show) who is estranged from her adult daughters, esp. her younger daughter Ruby, since she left her husband and teenage daughters years ago. Ruby has amazingly never learned the true story of why Nora left and the book is about how the truth transforms her.<br /><br />I had a hard time getting into this book. The characters were unlikeable, especially at first, and the characterizations w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14061894952572575529">For my book club this month. Nora is a discredited advice columnist (think Dr. Laura with a newspaper column and a radio show) who is estranged from her adult daughters, esp. her younger daughter Ruby, since she left her husband and teenage daughters years ago. Ruby has amazingly never learned the true story of why Nora left and the book is about how the truth transforms her.<br /><br />I had a hard time getting into this book. The characters were unlikeable, especially at first, and the characterizations were overblown and stereotypical (dying gay man ostracized by his family, overwhelmed young mother, etc). I ended up thinking it was okay, only because I thought the author made some good observations about motherhood and marriage in the last 50 pages. But the plot was predictable and the writing sappy. I think a book of Nora's advice columns would be more enjoyable. It would make a great Lifetime movie though!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14061894952572575529">...more</a>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5548149314560267790">I loved this novel...Hannah knows how to take you on a trip that is unforgettable! She has a way of drawing you into the story as if you are there with them experiencing everything first hand!<br /><br />The characters are real and easy to relate to. Dealing with life issues all of us have faced at one time or another it was easy to identify with what was going on.<br /><br />Love of family and the forgivness of choices made in the past that affected everyone. This is what it's about and I understood what was happening inside the hearts of each person...not a book that you'll be able to put down. <br /><br />As the story progressed, I couldn't read fast enough. I was laughing, crying, shouting, and cheering for these characters.<br /><br />Loved, loved, loved this book.<br /><br />Way to go Kristin...I'm a fan of yours and will keep reading your stories!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16908576577089735338">I had enjoyed the first book that I read by this author <a title="Magic Hour by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1470232.Magic_Hour">Magic Hour</a>, but I think that was mostly due to the subject matter (feral children). This book shared similarities in that it too was about families and children. And also that the family was so unrealistic...<br />Still, it was an enjoyable and certainly escapist-fast read. I will most likely read more by her - though I doubt I will ever rush out just to get one.<br />In many ways, this author is reminiscent of <a title="Jodi Picoult" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7128.Jodi_Picoult">Jodi Picoult</a> - though on a more superfici</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16908576577089735338">I had enjoyed the first book that I read by this author <a title="Magic Hour by Kristin Hannah" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1470232.Magic_Hour">Magic Hour</a>, but I think that was mostly due to the subject matter (feral children). This book shared similarities in that it too was about families and children. And also that the family was so unrealistic...<br />Still, it was an enjoyable and certainly escapist-fast read. I will most likely read more by her - though I doubt I will ever rush out just to get one.<br />In many ways, this author is reminiscent of <a title="Jodi Picoult" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7128.Jodi_Picoult">Jodi Picoult</a> - though on a more superficial, beach-read type of level.<br />Still, I would recommend it to anyone looking for a sappy, sentimental-type book.</span>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer241292187">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6225202852349819486">I'm not sure whether to give this book a 3 or a 4. On one hand I really enjoyed the story, on the other hand, the characters made me really angry! I really disliked how Nora expected such forgiveness from her daughters and wasn't really willing to share with them the true reasons behind her pain and what was going on in the early part of their lives. I felt that she was awful to Ruby and made her feel guilty and like a horrible person for shutting her mother out when she was the one who in fact</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6225202852349819486">I'm not sure whether to give this book a 3 or a 4. On one hand I really enjoyed the story, on the other hand, the characters made me really angry! I really disliked how Nora expected such forgiveness from her daughters and wasn't really willing to share with them the true reasons behind her pain and what was going on in the early part of their lives. I felt that she was awful to Ruby and made her feel guilty and like a horrible person for shutting her mother out when she was the one who in fact ran out on them. I'm glad that they were eventually able to resolve their issues and i enjoyed reading how their relationship was mended but I didn't like the way Kristin Hannah created such weak female characters. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer198963535">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17936621614393871177">Alright, so these are definitely in the beach-read category (or transfusion room category, if that's where you're needing to pass time ...) But for beach reads, I really think Hannah does a good job with developing characters and relationships. I liked this book a lot--I'd give it a 3.5 if I could. I liked the mother-daughter relationship, and the way that the daughter had to sort of re-visit what went on in her childhood in order to come to terms with that past. I think we're all like that. Thi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17936621614393871177">Alright, so these are definitely in the beach-read category (or transfusion room category, if that's where you're needing to pass time ...) But for beach reads, I really think Hannah does a good job with developing characters and relationships. I liked this book a lot--I'd give it a 3.5 if I could. I liked the mother-daughter relationship, and the way that the daughter had to sort of re-visit what went on in her childhood in order to come to terms with that past. I think we're all like that. Things look very different to young kids than to adults. And often part of the healing process comes from re-meeting your parents as peers.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GPDhyOSPFYaXinima924KbXFzmzvKxCPvxcM8jRBvDZ9JN4bFl0BfBtSDB0VvF6b/DINdab2VyXVHglg+NRKcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GDjCHBt1/hlQ6dgwPrDPEtMnqi9fxsOBm9e4dxcSwrV97P3P6afq49wxrItA0SmgmtBpNhYbhCvx3r3l24c08A==')})
  }

But now Lily, the baby of the family, is sending Abbie urgent emails begging her to return home to Nantucket. Their middle sister, Emma, has taken to her bed, emotionally devastated after the loss of her high-powered stockbroker’s job and a shockingly unexpected break-up with her fiancé. Also, Lily is deeply worried that Marina, the beautiful, enigmatic woman renting their guesthouse, has set her sights on the sisters’ widowed father, Jim. The Fox girls closed ranks years ago after the haunting, untimely death of their mother, but seeing their dad move on with his life forces each of them to take stock. Over the course of the summer, the sisters’ lives grow as turbulent as the unpredictable currents encircling Nantucket. When Abbie encounters an incredibly appealing married man, she breaks her own rules in the name of love, fearing all the while that she’ll regret it. Meanwhile, type-A Emma learns a new definition of success, and strong-minded Lily must reconcile her dreams with reality. Even Marina, who has come to Nantucket to forget heartbreak and betrayal, faces an astonishing turn of events that will find her torn between fate and freedom. Their careers are flourishing—Molly is a horticulturist and Robin is a world-class runner—and they are in the prime of their lives. So when Molly receives the news that Robin has suffered a massive heart attack, she couldn’t be more shocked. At the hospital, the Snow family receives a grim prognosis: Robin may never regain consciousness.As Robin’s parents and siblings struggle to cope, the complex nature of their relationship is put to the ultimate test. Molly has always lived in Robin’s shadow and her feelings for her have run the gamut, from love to resentment and back. The last time they spoke, they argued. But now there is so much more at stake. Molly’s parents fold under the devastating circumstances, and her brother retreats into the cool reserve that is shattering his own family. It’s up to Molly to make the tough decisions, and she soon makes discoveries that destroy some of her most cherished beliefs about the sister she thought she knew. Once again New York Times bestselling author Barbara Delinsky brings us a masterful family portrait, filled with thought-provoking ideas about the nature of life itself, how emotions affect the     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah">About Kristin Hannah</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/54493.Kristin_Hannah"><img alt="54493" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1417050721p2/54493.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer11275003854997841372">Kristin Hannah is the New York Times bestselling author of twenty-one novels, including the blockbuster Firefly Lane and #1 bestsellers Night Road and Home Front. She is a former lawyer turned writer and is the mother of one son. She lives in the Pacific Northwest and Hawaii with her husband.</span>

    </div>
